Close
fainted; Nausea; lips white; Really pale; 12 year old daughter; This is a spontaneous report from a contactable consumer (patient's mother). A 12-years-old female patient received BNT162B2 (PFIZER-BIONTECH COVID-19 VACCINE), dose 1 via an unspecified route of administration, administered in Arm Left on 14May2021 got it closer to 12:00 (Batch/Lot number was reported: First letter was R, W or B, followed by A6256) at the age of 12-years-old as SINGLE DOSE for covid-19 immunization. The COVID-19 vaccine was administered at Pharmacy/Drug Store. Medical history reported as none. No family medical history relevant to adverse event, reporter who was the patients mother, is a fainter, who fainted a lot when she saw blood. The patient's concomitant medications were not reported. The patient did not receive any other vaccines within 4 weeks prior to the COVID vaccine. As they were driving away, her daughter started feeling really nauseous, then fainted, was super pale, lips were white and she was really pale. It all occurred at the same time all started 10 minutes after vaccine on 14May2021. Then the ambulance came. Her daughter looked really bad and it freaked reporter out. Her daughter sat for a little while and was feeling better now. Her daughter was no longer pale, it went away. They checked her and everything was normal. No Emergency Room and no Physician Office visit required. Ambulance was called, they checked her and she was fine. Told her to keep any eye on her at home. The outcome of the events pale, lips were white was recovered on 14May2021, the outcome of the events nauseous, and fainted was recovering. Information about Lot/Batch number has been requested.
12 2021-05-27 nausea It was within 5 minutes, she started having hives that went down her arm and spread to other arm, fa... Read more
Close
It was within 5 minutes, she started having hives that went down her arm and spread to other arm, face, trunk, legs, stomach. I went and got a nurse and she called a pediatric team - three nurses and one doctor - they took her vitals and gave her some Benadryl - 30 ML (children's). They had her sit and drink a bottle of water. We watched to see if the swelling and the hives would shrink and go away. It was probably about 20 minutes later where they went away, but she developed a headache and she was nauseated. We administered Benadryl (gave her regular 25 mg tablet every 6 hours) for the next 24 hors in the dosage times. She was nauseated the first day and she had headache for two days. The hives went away by the time she went to bed the evening of the vaccine.

Close
She was taking Claritin for the few days before this event. She normally takes it every fall and every spring. She had seasonal allergy symptoms on the days leading up to this event- she had sore throat, runny nose, a little headache and congestion and developed a cough; on the day of this symptoms she spiked a low grade fever - 100.5. I did a rapid test for COVID at home which was negative for her. Sudden onset: A bunch of knives poking her on the inside of her stomach - pokey from hips to ribs. She started to double over and bend over. Within 10 minutes, she couldn't stand up. She was telling me that something was really wrong. This isn't her character so I knew it was very wrong. I took her to ER. I was still concerned about appendicitis or COVID. This episode lasted for 90 minutes and then it came and went for the rest of the night and then after that - she had runny nose and congestion (normal allergies after that). She was better before they gave her the medication but it didn't seem like she really needed them. She was improving before she got either of the medications: Zofran; Levsin. They gave her a dosage of each there and sent home with a prescription but we never had them filled as she was feeling better. - As it started to improve - it ( being the pokey pain) it was located closer to her ribs and breastbone.

did well acted right, felt right up until 5 AM this morning (6/4/21), she woke up throwing up over and over again, she couldn?t keep even a dissolvable Zofran down. > I immediately contacted her Hematologist and he told me to take her to the E.R. > blood disorder, ?Hereditary Spherocytosis? came to life, flared up. >got extremely sick, where she could not walk or stand by 8:00 am this morning, when we arrived at the E.R. she had to be placed in a wheelchair because she was so weak. > Fluids, Pain medicine, Motrin, and nausea medication were given, plus rotating cool rags on her head to get her body temperature down. > CBC, was off the charts, she has developed Anemia and was diagnosed this morning. > blood pressure dropped to 91/42. > I spoke with two hematologist on top of speaking with the 2 E.R. Doctors. >reached over 110% immunity if not more. > Both Hematologist I spoke with plus the E.R. doctors determined she was at 100% immunity with just the first dose. > Due to her reaction her Oncologist/Hematologist are communicating with other hematologist in the U.S. about a reaction of a ?12 year old pediatric patient with Hereditary Spherocytosis?, further research will begin according to the Director of Onoccologist/Hematologist in the next few weeks to help other pediatric patients with Heriditary Spherocytosis in the U.S., the main point of this research is determining that one dose of Covid vaccine reaches 100% immunity vs 2 doses which would be equivalent to ?2 doses plus 2 booster shots of Covid vaccine? to someone with hereditary spherocytosis. > > After 8 hours of going through this, she was able to walk and stand. She was back to her old self. > If you can please reach out to CDC and let them know about a 12 year olds patient with Hereditary Spherocytosis reaction to second dose of Phizer Vaccine.

Patient is a 13-year-old who was transferred from another hospital for chest pain in the setting of Covid vaccination. She received her second dose of Pfizer vaccine on Tuesday, June 29. On Wednesday she developed fatigue chest pain shortness of breath weakness, nausea and mild abdominal pain. She also had a fever to 102.5 Fahrenheit. mom is a nurse and took her pulse and felt that it was 30 and fast. She then took 1 with her home equipment it was in the 120s. She called her neighbor who took her pulse and it was in the 130s. She then transferred her to another Hospital for further care at hospital her vital sinus evaluation was a temperature of 37.4 pulse 119 respiratory rate is 15 blood pressure 106/62 satting 98% on room air. On exam she was well appearing with tenderness to palpation of sternum heart rate normal rate and rhythm lungs clear bilaterally and abdominal exam benign. they obtain CBC with white count of 4.8 hemoglobin 12.9 Camm that was unremarkable LFTs are within normal limits troponin that was negative BNP 223 with a normal upper limit of 125 ESR 2 D-dimer 0.697 with upper limit of normal 0.5 and a CRP of 9 with upper limit of normal of 8.1. UA bland. She was given Toradol for chest pain EKG with sinus tachycardia . She was given 1/2 L normal saline bolus ondansetron Toradol and started on maintenance IV fluids of D5 NS. She was then transferred to another hospital for further care . Upon arrival here she notes improvement in her energy level and all of her pain except for her chest pain. She describes it as a pressure on top of her chest that is right in the center and is worse with movement and deep breaths. Of note she had a appendectomy a few years ago that was complicated by surgeons making the bowel and then required her to have a bowel resection. She has no dietary restrictions and eats by mouth, no GI complications in the long-term. PMH: as above PSH: No significant past surgical history FH: Reviewed and noncontributory to current presentation SH: Lives with caregivers Meds: None Allergies: No known drug allergies Immunizations: UTD Review of Systems Constitutional: fever, no chills, no sweats, fatigue Skin: no rash, no lesions, Eye: no redness ENMT: no ear pain, no sore throat, no congestion, no hoarseness Respiratory: + shortness of breath, no cough, no wheezing Cardiovascular: + chest pain, no palpitations, Gastrointestinal: + nausea, no vomiting, no diarrhea, no GI bleeding Genitourinary: no dysuria, no hematuria, Musculoskeletal: + muscle pain, Neurologic: no headache, no dizziness, no numbness, no weakness Psychiatric: no sleeping problems, Allergy/Immunologic: no recurrent infections, Additional ROS info: All other systems of a 10 system review are negative. Briefly, patient is presenting with chest pain, myalgias, and fever in setting of recent covid vaccine (2nd dose Pfizer 2 days ago). Seen at an outside hospital where labs were notable for mildly elevated BNP and D-dimer, negative troponin, normal LFTs and chemistries. Chest x-ray reportedly negative. EKG with T wave inversions in V1 through V4 (read as nonspecific ST changes by their physician), but otherwise normal. Given the possibility of post Covid vaccine myocarditis or PE, transferred for further management. Patient states that after Toradol that she received the outside hospital all of her other symptoms have resolved but she continues to have chest pain. My exam showed: Gen: tired but nontoxic appearing, no acute distress, alert and active; HEENT: PERRL, EOMI, normal conjunctiva, neck supple without LAN; Chest: significant reproducible chest pain; Card: RRR, no murmur, good perfusion, brisk radial pulses bilaterally; Lungs: CTAB, good air entry, no increased WOB; Abd: soft, non-tender, non-distended, no masses; Ext: warm and well perfused, moving all extremities; Skin: no rashes Chest pain. Overall well appearing with normal exam with reproducible tenderness. Given recent Covid vaccine, must consider myocarditis, although only mildly elevated BNP and negative troponin at the outside hospital are reassuring, especially given reproducible pain and reassuring EKG. Symptoms then may represent musculoskeletal etiology such as costochondritis or myositis related to vaccination. Less likely pneumonia or pneumothorax, but possible. Low suspicion for PE given lack of persistent tachycardia (tachycardia improved while in ED, currently HR 80s) or hypoxia. EKG obtained which showed T wave inversions in V1-V4 (normal for age). Bedside ultrasound with normal global function and lack of pericardial effusion. Labs obtained in BCH ED notable for negative BNP and troponin, along with reassuring lipase given abdominal pain. Thus, unlikely to be true myocarditis, more likely musculoskeletal etiology such as costochondritis or chest wall pain. Cardiology will discuss with mom for reassurance. Final Diagnosis 1. Shortness of breath R06.00 PLEASE NOTE: Since the patient is not from here, we do not have access to her vaccination records and cannot supply lot number, etc.

14 2021-07-21 nausea Ten minutes post immunization, the patient became pale and was complaining of dizziness, nausea, and... Read more
Close
Ten minutes post immunization, the patient became pale and was complaining of dizziness, nausea, and feeling lightheaded. Nursing staff evaluating patient when witnessed, syncopal episode occurred. Episode lasted for less than 15 seconds with no injury to patient. Patient was in a seated position at time of event and was then placed supine with legs elevated. No incontinence and patient remembers everything up to and following the brief episode of syncope. (Patient has a previous history of syncope following HPV9 immunization.) Once supine, patient's pallor improved as well as other symptoms. At 10:20 am, repeat vital signs taken in the seated position: HR 80 (regular and strong), RR 20 (non-labored), BP 100/54 (left arm). Patient denied any complaints at this time. Patient stated that she had a small amount of chocolate pudding for breakfast. Denied any issues with blood sugar. Patient was given and consumed peanut butter crackers, Munchkin donuts, and water without difficulty. She did not drink the protein shake, but chose to take it home with her. Dr. was notified of the event and followed up with patient and father. Patient was monitored for another 30 minutes. Vital signs at 10:35 am: HR 84 (strong and regular), RR 20 (non-labored), BP 110/62 (Right arm). Skin color back to normal. No complaints. No dizziness, lightheadedness, or feeling faint when standing. Gait normal. Patient instructed to always notify health care staff of history of syncope after injections and to always wait at least 30 minutes for delayed symptoms. Patient discharged to home with father. No complaints or concerns. Follow up call placed at 5:45 pm and patient out and about with mother, no complaints. Family notified to call back with any questions or concerns.

My daughter received her second Pfizer vaccinations at 2:15 pm. At 1230 at night she work up with stabbing chest pain in the center of her chest that lasted three hours. She initially said her felt faint and couldn?t catch her breath as well as initial nausea. Being an advanced healthcare professional, I spent five minutes of asking her questions: did she eat something bad, did she feel like she needed and inhaler, did she need to use the restroom, checked her pulse (100bpm with palpitations), no resolve. We live 5 minutes from hospital where we prefer to go, but my daughter didn?t think she could make the five minute ride there. We went to ER that is around the block from us and it was total chaos. 40 + people in the waiting room to be seen. My daughter was visibly in distress, crying and couldn?t keep still because of the intense chest pain she rated a 10 out of 10. Finally they did a 12 lead EKG. The rolled us to the back of the waiting room. After 15 minutes, I rolled back out to the front desk and no attention to her and her severe chest pain. Finally I announced we were going to hospital. The called back to us? ?Good Luck!? Got pt to hospital and the immediately did EKG, lab work, chest x ray, urinalysis. The chest pain became intermittent then final subsided. The doctors ruled out pneumonia, No PE, EKG WNL, lab work fine. The Doctor stated it was chest wall pain and gave us a NSAID prescription. I talked to my sister who is an nurse works in the vaccination clinics. She said she has had patients who have had bouts of pericarditis and pleurisy after the second shot. That motivated me to google second dose Pfizer reaction in teens. There is a rare side effect of myocarditis in the teen population after the second dose. The publication date was June 4 the day before my daughters reaction. I didn?t thinsk the ER physician was aware of the the possible rare side effect of myocarditis in teens. I was happy with the care we did receive.

Close
Client received dose 1 of the COVID19 Pfizer vaccine (Lot# EW0187 Exp 08/31/21) at 13:32 from RN1. RN1 reported that within 5 seconds of receiving the vaccine, the client reported she felt dizzy and experienced a syncopal episode for 2-3 seconds. As the syncopal episode was occurring, ancillary staff, requested RN2 radio for a Lead Nurse & EMT. At 13:34 Lead RN arrived at station 6, radioed for an EMT, and observed client sitting up in the vaccination chair being held by her mother and RN1. Lead RN noted client?s head was down with her eyes open, exhibiting pallor and was diaphoretic. Lead RN asked client her name and how she was feeling. Client did not respond. Co-Lead RN entered the room at 13:35. RN1, Lead RN, Co-Lead RN, and client?s mother guided client to the floor, laid her in a supine position, lifting her legs and feet on a chair. Co-Lead RN removed client?s mask, continued to ask client her name. Within 2-3 seconds of repositioning client, she became responsive and alert & oriented to person, place, time, and event. Client also immediately stated, ?I?m fine.? EMT1, EMT2, and EMT3 came to the station at 13:36 with a zero-gravity chair. The EMTs assisted client into the zero-gravity chair. Client?s mother stated client has no underlying health conditions, no allergies, and that birth control is the only medication the client takes. The client confirmed this by nodding her head in agreeance. EMT2 gave client a bottle of water and the client immediately started drinking the water. Lead RN asked client if she had eaten or drank anything today. Client?s mother stated she did not realize her daughter had not eaten or drank anything prior to coming to get vaccinated. Client stated she was given a granola bar downstairs at check-in and ate it before receiving the vaccine. At 13:45 EMT1 took vitals. Both EMT1 & EMT2 were unable to obtain client?s blood pressure (HR:61, O2Sat: 97%). Lead RN asked client and her mother what the client?s normal blood pressure is. Client and her mother did not know, and client?s mother indicated that the client is an athlete in good shape. At 13:48, EMT3 took client?s blood pressure, which was 100/60. Client?s mother stated client was anxious about being vaccinated and has fainted when anxious in the past, but the last time was around 5 years ago. Client stated she was feeling better and no longer feeling dizzy. Client stated she just ?feels hot.? Lead RN brought client an ice pack to put behind her neck and damp paper towels to wipe her face with. At 13:59 EMT3 took client?s vitals (BP: 118/70, HR: 65, O2Sat 98%). Lead RN observed that client?s color was returning to her face and client was less diaphoretic. Client finished her bottled water and was given another by EMT2, which she started drinking. Lead RN asked client if she felt she could stand up. Client stood up and stated she was ?feeling fine.? At 14:05 all 3 EMTs escorted client and her mother to the observation room where she was monitored for an additional 30 minutes. At 14:30 Lead RN went to the observation room where EMT1was taking client?s vitals (BP: 110/70, HR: 60, SPO2 Sat 98%). Lead RN observed that client?s color had fully returned, and client was no longer diaphoretic. Client stated she ?felt fine? and was hungry. Client?s mother stated she would take client to get something to eat and EMT2 gave client an additional snack that client took with her when she left. Client and her mother left at 14:30. Client was walking with a steady gait when she exited the building.

Attendee received first dose Pfizer vaccine at 15:08 in the left arm. Lot# FA6780. Attendee was directed to observation area. At 15:10 fainted in her chair x 20 seconds, her parents were by her side and she did not fall out of the chair. When she aroused she reported feeling lightheaded, dizzy, mild nausea and ring in the ears. Attendee's skin was cool, clammy, and pale. Cot brought to the patient area. Attendee assisted to the cot to lie down, legs elevated. Icepack applied to her neck. 15:13 HR: 88 BP: 108/58 RR: 14 O2Sat%: 97 Temp: 97.0

7-19-2021, five hours after receiving the vaccine, her mother states she developed a "severe headache" and vomited. 7-20-2021, in the afternoon, mother states patient became dizzy, passed out, hitting chin on concrete floor and became unconscious. Mother drove patient to ER, mother states that it took 20-30 mins before she regained consciousness. Patient was released from ER and followed up with PCP the next day.

Within 5 minutes of receiving vaccination, the patient began to feel like she was dreaming and passed out while she was seated. We moved the patient to the floor where she regained consciousness . The patient had further complaints of numbness in the arms, light- headedness and was nauseated and vomited. 911 was called and responded, and the patient said she was ok and did not want to go to hospital.
